## First important point: the model *is* saved
`train_dlc_multi_mouse_engine.py` does **not** save a separate custom checkpoint file because **DLC itself saves the trained model snapshots inside the project folder** during training/evaluation.

In your case, the model lives in the DLC project directory under something like:

- `dlc_synth_project/dlc-models/iteration-0/.../train/snapshot-*`

and your evaluation log explicitly says it used:

- **`snapshot-200000`**

So the trained model is already there; in DLC, the **`config.yaml` is the key** used to find and apply the correct trained network. The DLC docs describe `config.yaml` as the project anchor and show video analysis via `deeplabcut.analyze_videos(...)`. citeturn1view0turn2view0

---

## Your intended workflow (correct)
Your proposed workflow is the right one:

- **Training data generation phase**  
  `mouse_sim2.py` + `mouse_deform_render..._dlc...py` (with labels/project generation)

- **Inference/evaluation phase on new synthetic data**  
  `mouse_sim2.py` (new seed) + renderer (videos only, labels ignored/not needed)  
  → then **DLC `analyze_videos`** on the new videos

That separation is exactly how you should use a trained DLC model.

---

## How to run prediction / extract 2D body parts on new videos

### A) Generate new videos (new seed)
Use your existing simulation/render pipeline, but with a **different `--seed`** (and ideally similar camera settings/domain).

You do **not** need to generate DLC labels for inference videos.

---

### B) Run DLC analysis on those videos
For multi-animal DLC, the standard entry point is:

- `deeplabcut.analyze_videos(config_path, videos, ..., auto_track=True)`

The maDLC guide explicitly notes that **new videos do not need to be added to `config.yaml`**, and you can pass either exact video paths or a folder. With `auto_track=True`, DLC chains pose estimation + tracking + stitching and writes the familiar output files (`.h5`, optionally `.csv`). citeturn2view0turn2view1

### Minimal Python script (recommended)
Use this for your new rendered videos (3 cameras):

```python
# predict_dlc_multimouse_videos.py
import deeplabcut as dlc

config = "/media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/dlc_synth_project/config.yaml"

videos = [
    "/path/to/new_render/cam1_top.mp4",
    "/path/to/new_render/cam2_front.mp4",
    "/path/to/new_render/cam3_side.mp4",
]

# Multi-animal prediction + tracking (assembled per-animal tracks)
dlc.analyze_videos(
    config,
    videos,
    videotype=".mp4",
    shuffle=1,
    save_as_csv=True,      # also write CSV in addition to HDF5
    auto_track=True,       # important for maDLC tracked output
    n_tracks=2,            # two mice
    animal_names=["mouse0", "mouse1"],  # optional but useful
    destfolder="/path/to/new_render/dlc_predictions",
    gputouse=0,            # TensorFlow engine GPU index (optional)
    TFGPUinference=True,   # default for TF engine; explicit here
)

# Optional sanity checks
dlc.create_labeled_video(
    config,
    videos,
    videotype=".mp4",
    shuffle=1,
    destfolder="/path/to/new_render/dlc_predictions",
)

dlc.plot_trajectories(
    config,
    videos,
    videotype=".mp4",
    shuffle=1,
    destfolder="/path/to/new_render/dlc_predictions",
)
```

### Run it
```bash
conda activate dlc_mouse
python predict_dlc_multimouse_videos.py
```

---

## What files you get (the actual 2D predictions)
With `auto_track=True`, maDLC writes tracked predictions to **HDF5** (and CSV if `save_as_csv=True`) in the video directory or `destfolder`. The docs describe `analyze_videos` output as HDF/CSV pose labels and note that `save_as_csv=True` exports CSV too. citeturn2view1

### For your downstream 3D step, use:
- **`.h5`** (best, preserves MultiIndex cleanly)
- or **`.csv`** (human-readable, easier to inspect)

In multi-animal tracked outputs, the columns are typically a **pandas MultiIndex** with levels like:
- scorer
- individual (`mouse0`, `mouse1`)
- bodypart
- coord (`x`, `y`, `likelihood`)

That is exactly the structure you want before triangulation / bundle adjustment.

---

## Important distinction (maDLC)
If you set `auto_track=False`, `analyze_videos` first produces raw detections (pickle), and you must run:
- `convert_detections2tracklets(...)`
- `stitch_tracklets(...)`

The maDLC docs explicitly explain this split and recommend `auto_track=True` for the common workflow. citeturn2view0turn2view1

For your use case (2 mice, synthetic videos, direct extraction of 2D tracks), **`auto_track=True` is the right choice**.

---

## Where prediction results should go (recommended)
For clean organization (especially for later 3D reconstruction), I’d store outputs per simulation seed:

```text
out_seed_17/
  cam1_top.mp4
  cam2_front.mp4
  cam3_side.mp4
  dlc_predictions/
    cam1_topDLC_...h5
    cam1_topDLC_...csv
    cam2_frontDLC_...h5
    cam2_frontDLC_...csv
    cam3_sideDLC_...h5
    cam3_sideDLC_...csv
    (labeled videos / trajectories, if requested)
```

The maDLC guide includes filtering and labeled-video steps in the standard workflow. citeturn1view0turn2view1

User: For DLC we generated a conda environment with two hooks. Can we store this in an environment.yml - just in case it has to be generated again?

Assistant: Yes — **partly**.

You can (and should) store **most of the DLC environment** in an `environment.yml`, but there are **two important limitations**:

## What *can* go into `environment.yml`
- conda packages (e.g. `python`, `pip`, `cudatoolkit=11.8`)
- pip packages (e.g. `deeplabcut`, `tensorflow`, `tensorpack`, `tf_slim`, `nvidia-cudnn-cu11`)
- simple environment variables (e.g. `PYTHONNOUSERSITE=1`) via `variables:`

## What *cannot reliably* go into `environment.yml`
- your **activate/deactivate hook scripts** (the shell scripts under `etc/conda/activate.d/` / `deactivate.d/`)
- the **dynamic `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` logic** that computes the pip `nvidia.cudnn` wheel path
- the **intentional final override** `typing_extensions==4.15.0` after installing TF 2.12 (this conflicts with TF’s declared pin and is best applied as a post-step)

So the best reproducible setup is:

1. `environment.yml` (base env + most packages)
2. `post_setup.sh` (final pip override for `typing_extensions`)
3. `activate.d` / `deactivate.d` hook scripts (kept in your repo and copied into the env)

---

# Recommended structure

```text
dlc_env/
  environment_dlc_tf_gpu.yml
  post_setup_dlc_tf_gpu.sh
  hooks/
    activate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh
    deactivate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh
```

---

# 1) Example `environment_dlc_tf_gpu.yml` (base + GPU runtimes, no hooks)

```yaml
name: dlc_mouse
channels:
  - conda-forge
dependencies:
  - python=3.10
  - pip
  - cudatoolkit=11.8
  - pip:
      - deeplabcut==2.3.11
      - tensorflow==2.12.1
      - tensorpack
      - tf_slim
      - nvidia-cudnn-cu11==8.6.0.163
      # Optional but usually already pulled:
      # - pandas
      # - tables
      # - opencv-python
variables:
  PYTHONNOUSERSITE: "1"
```

### Why no `typing_extensions==4.15.0` here?
Because this conflicts with TF 2.12’s declared requirement (`<4.6`) and may make pip resolution fail in a single transaction. You already found the working pattern:

- install TF
- then **override** `typing_extensions` afterward

So that should stay in a **post-setup step**.

---

# 2) Post-setup script (important)
This reproduces the working final state you have now.

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

# Usage: ./post_setup_dlc_tf_gpu.sh dlc_mouse
ENV_NAME="${1:-dlc_mouse}"

conda activate "$ENV_NAME"

# DLC + TF 2.12 work, but torch import via DLC needs newer typing_extensions.
python -m pip install --upgrade "typing_extensions==4.15.0"
```

---

# 3) Keep the hooks as files in your repo
You already have working hook scripts. Keep them under version control and copy them into the env after creation.

### Activate hook (`hooks/activate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh`)
Use the version you have now (the working one that sets `PYTHONNOUSERSITE=1` and prepends `CONDA_PREFIX/lib` + pip cuDNN path to `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`).

### Deactivate hook (`hooks/deactivate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh`)
Use the corrected version you fixed.

---

# 4) Recreate the environment later (full recipe)
```bash
conda env create -f environment_dlc_tf_gpu.yml
conda activate dlc_mouse

# install hooks
mkdir -p "$CONDA_PREFIX/etc/conda/activate.d" "$CONDA_PREFIX/etc/conda/deactivate.d"
cp hooks/activate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh "$CONDA_PREFIX/etc/conda/activate.d/"
cp hooks/deactivate.d/dlc_mouse_env.sh "$CONDA_PREFIX/etc/conda/deactivate.d/"

# re-activate to apply hooks
conda deactivate
conda activate dlc_mouse

# final compatibility override
./post_setup_dlc_tf_gpu.sh dlc_mouse
```

---

## Practical recommendation
Store all three pieces (YAML + hooks + post-setup script).  
That is much more robust than trying to force everything into a single `environment.yml`.

If you want, I can generate these three files for you (ready to save in your repo) with the exact hook contents you’re currently using.

User: should I create my own environment.yml with conda env export > environment.yml or should I use the much shorter example you suggest above (it is only a proposal, isn't)?

Assistant: Use the **short, curated YAML** (plus hooks + post-setup script), **not** a raw `conda env export > environment.yml`, at least not as your primary reproducibility file.

## Why not `conda env export` as the main file
A full export will include:
- hundreds of transitive packages
- platform-specific build strings
- exact versions that are often unnecessarily brittle
- pip-resolved packages that may reflect temporary conflicts/workarounds
- possibly packages pulled in indirectly that you don’t actually care about

That makes it:
- harder to solve on another machine
- harder to maintain
- harder to understand
- more likely to break in the future for irrelevant reasons

So yes: my shorter YAML was a **proposal**, and the right idea is to create your **own curated version** based on what actually mattered in your successful setup.

---

## Best practice (what I recommend)
Keep **two files**:

### 1) `environment_dlc_tf_gpu.yml` (curated, human-maintained) ✅ primary
This is what you use to recreate the env.

### 2) `environment_dlc_tf_gpu.lockish.yml` (optional snapshot export) 📦 reference only
Generated by `conda env export` for forensic/debug purposes, not for routine recreation.

That gives you both:
- reproducibility intent (curated file)
- exact historical record (full export)

---

## What to put in the curated YAML
Use the short version style, but tailor it to your now-proven setup:
- Python 3.10
- `cudatoolkit=11.8` (conda)
- pip installs:
  - `deeplabcut==2.3.11`
  - `tensorflow==2.12.1`
  - `tensorpack`
  - `tf_slim`
  - `nvidia-cudnn-cu11==8.6.0.163`
- `PYTHONNOUSERSITE=1` in `variables:`

Then keep the following outside the YAML:
- activate/deactivate hooks (for `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` and env hygiene)
- post-setup `typing_extensions==4.15.0` override

That reflects the real constraints you discovered.

---

## When `conda env export` *is* useful
Use it:
- as a **backup snapshot**
- to inspect exact versions after a working install
- to diff two states of the environment
- for debugging (“what changed?”)

### If you do export, prefer this (less noisy)
```bash
conda env export --from-history > environment_from_history.yml
```

This only captures packages you explicitly requested via conda (e.g. `python`, `pip`, `cudatoolkit`) and avoids the giant dependency dump.

But note: it won’t include the important pip-installed DLC/TF packages in a complete way unless you maintain them explicitly.

---

(dlc_mouse) hellwich@Artemis:~/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/dlc_mouse$

Assistant: You’re hitting a **known DLC 2.3.x inference gotcha**: `analyze_videos()` is trying to read `cfg["batch_size"]` from the **project `config.yaml`**, but your `config.yaml` doesn’t contain that key, so it crashes with:

- `KeyError: 'batch_size'`

### Why it happens
Your training config (pose_cfg) had a batch size, but **DLC’s TF inference code path in 2.3.11** sometimes expects `batch_size` to exist in the *project* `config.yaml` as well, and it doesn’t if the project was created in certain ways.

---

## Fix options
### Option 1 (cleanest): patch project config once
Add this line to:

`dlc_synth_project/config.yaml`

```yaml
batch_size: 8
```

Then rerun prediction.

### Option 2 (script-side fix): pass `batchsize` and/or auto-patch config
I updated the batch predictor script to do both:
- pass `batchsize=<N>` into `analyze_videos` (if supported)
- **auto-add `batch_size:` to config.yaml if it’s missing**

### Updated script
Download and use this version:

- [predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch.py)

---

## How to run (your exact case)
```bash
conda activate dlc_mouse
python predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch.py \
  --config /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/dlc_synth_project/config.yaml \
  --videos-dir /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render \
  --destfolder /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions \
  --n-tracks 2 \
  --batchsize 8 \
  --create-labeled-video
```

By default it will also try to patch `batch_size` into the project config if missing.

Assistant: That crash is the **same class of problem as the earlier `batch_size` one**: DLC’s TF multi-animal inference path assumes the **project** `config.yaml` has certain keys, and your project config doesn’t include them.

Now it fails at:

- `KeyError: 'cropping'` (inside `predict_multianimal.py`)

### What DLC expects
In DLC 2.3.11, TF maDLC inference reads from the **project config.yaml** keys like:

- `batch_size`
- `cropping` (boolean)

Your project was created without those keys, so inference crashes.

---

## Fix: use a predictor script that auto-patches missing config keys
I produced an updated version that **patches `config.yaml` in-place** (using `ruamel.yaml` if available, so formatting/comments are preserved):

- adds `batch_size: <your --batchsize>`
- adds `cropping: false`
- (also adds `x1/x2/y1/y2` defaults, harmless unless cropping is enabled)

### Download/use this script
- [predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch_v3.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch_v3.py)

---

## Run it (your exact command)
```bash
conda activate dlc_mouse

python predict_dlc_multi_mouse_batch_v3.py \
  --config /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/dlc_synth_project/config.yaml \
  --videos-dir /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render \
  --destfolder /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions \
  --n-tracks 2 \
  --batchsize 8 \
  --create-labeled-video
```

On first run, you should see something like:
- `[compat] patched config.yaml (added defaults): batch_size, cropping, x1, x2, y1, y2`

Then inference should proceed.

```yaml
batch_size: 8
cropping: false
```

But the v3 script handles it automatically.

Here’s why, line by line (and what you should take away):

## What’s working correctly
- **Config patching** worked:  
  `patched config.yaml (added defaults): batch_size, cropping, x1, x2, y1, y2`

- **GPU inference is active**:
  - `Created device ... GPU:0 ...`
  - `Loaded cuDNN version 8600`

- **All 3 videos were analyzed** end-to-end:
  - cam1_top: 1800/1800 frames (~40 fps)
  - cam2_front: 1800/1800 frames (~49 fps)
  - cam3_side: 1800/1800 frames (~48 fps)

- **Outputs were saved** in your `dlc_predictions` folder for each camera:
  - `.h5` per video (pose detections)
  - plus tracklet/tracking outputs (`stitch.py` wrote “tracks” to h5)

- **Labeled videos were successfully generated** for all 3 cameras (fast ~350 fps writing):
  - ends with `Done.`

So the pipeline is now: **render → analyze_videos → tracking artifacts → labeled video**, and it completes.

## What those “tracklets created … now stitch_tracklets” messages mean
DLC is telling you that it produced **tracklets** (short segments). It also ran a stitching step (you see `stitch.py` writing `df.to_hdf(..., "tracks")`), but DLC still prints its generic guidance message.

For your synthetic case, this is typically fine. If you later see identity swaps, you can run explicit stitching/refinement, but you already got a tracked output saved.

## What files to use as “the predicted 2D body parts”
In `out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions/` you should now see, per camera, files like:

- `cam1_topDLC_..._200000.h5`
- `cam2_frontDLC_..._200000.h5`
- `cam3_sideDLC_..._200000.h5`

and also **tracking outputs** (often named with `..._tracks.h5` or similar; DLC sometimes appends `filtered`, `el`, `tracks`, etc., depending on the path taken).

### Which one is best for downstream 3D?
Use the file that contains **assembled tracks** (MultiIndex columns with individuals/bodyparts). Quick check:

```bash
python - <<'PY'
import pandas as pd, glob
paths = sorted(glob.glob("/media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions/*.h5"))
print("H5 files:", *[p.split("/")[-1] for p in paths], sep="\n  ")
for p in paths[:3]:
    try:
        df = pd.read_hdf(p)
        print("\n==", p.split("/")[-1], "==")
        print("shape:", df.shape)
        print("columns levels:", getattr(df.columns, "nlevels", None))
        print("first 5 col entries:", list(df.columns[:5]))
        break
    except Exception as e:
        print("could not read", p, "->", e)
PY
```

- If `columns.nlevels` is 4–5 and includes `individuals`/`bodyparts`, that’s what you want for triangulation.

## Warnings you can ignore
All these are library warnings (pandas deprecations), not correctness failures:
- `FutureWarning ... groupby axis=1`
- `to_hdf keyword-only in pandas 3.0`
- `layer.apply deprecated`

They don’t affect your outputs.

## One small improvement you may want
Your script prints:
- `[compat] analyze_videos: dropped unsupported kwargs: ['batch_size', 'engine', 'reid']`

That’s fine. DLC is using the **project config `batch_size`** now (which we patched), so you’re covered.

- `cam3_side..._el.h5`

## What the other files are (quick mapping)

- `*_el.h5` / `*_el.csv`  
  **final exported locations** (the thing you want)

- `*_el_bp_labeled.mp4`  
  your **QC video** with predicted points overlaid

- `*_full.pickle`  
  raw detection output / intermediate results (usually not needed)

- `*_el.pickle`  
  “extracted locations” intermediate (you can ignore; H5/CSV are enough)

- `*_meta.pickle`  
  metadata about the analysis run

- `*_assemblies.pickle`  
  multi-animal “assembly” decisions (how detections were assigned/assembled)

For 3D work, stick to **`*_el.h5`** unless you need to debug tracking/identity issues.

---

- triangulate only frames where likelihood is above a threshold in at least 2 cameras

User: Yes, please give me the reader function.

Assistant: Here’s a robust “reader + normalizer” that loads your per-camera `*_el.h5` files and returns:

1) a **long-format DataFrame** with one row per `(frame, camera, individual, bodypart)` containing `x, y, likelihood`, and  
2) an optional **dense NumPy array** shaped `(T, C, I, B, 3)` = `(frames, cameras, individuals, bodyparts, (x,y,likelihood))`.

It’s designed for exactly the MultiIndex columns you showed:
`(scorer, individual, bodypart, coord)`.

```python
# dlc_read_multicam.py
from __future__ import annotations

from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd


def _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(h5_path: str | Path) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    DLC writes H5 in different keys depending on the function/path.
    For *_el.h5, pd.read_hdf(path) often works directly.
    This helper falls back to reading the first key that is a DataFrame.
    """
    h5_path = str(h5_path)
    try:
        df = pd.read_hdf(h5_path)
        if isinstance(df, pd.DataFrame):
            return df
    except (ValueError, KeyError):
        pass

    with pd.HDFStore(h5_path, mode="r") as store:
        for key in store.keys():
            obj = store.get(key)
            if isinstance(obj, pd.DataFrame):
                return obj

    raise RuntimeError(f"No DataFrame found in H5 file: {h5_path}")


def _ensure_expected_multindex(df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Ensure df.columns is a 4-level MultiIndex:
      level0: scorer
      level1: individual
      level2: bodypart
      level3: coord in {'x','y','likelihood'}
    """
    if not isinstance(df.columns, pd.MultiIndex) or df.columns.nlevels != 4:
        raise ValueError(
            f"Expected 4-level MultiIndex columns (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord). "
            f"Got: {type(df.columns)} with nlevels={getattr(df.columns, 'nlevels', None)}"
        )

    # Normalize coord naming (some DLC variants may use 'likelihood' consistently; keep as-is).
    coords = set(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(3)))
    needed = {"x", "y", "likelihood"}
    if not needed.issubset(coords):
        raise ValueError(f"Expected coord level to contain {needed}, got {sorted(coords)}")

    return df


def _stack_one_camera(df: pd.DataFrame, camera: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Convert wide DLC MultiIndex df to long format:
      frame, camera, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood
    """
    df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

    # Stack to long: index -> frame, columns -> multiindex
    long = df.stack(level=[0, 1, 2])  # leaves coord as columns (x/y/likelihood)
    # After stack, long is a DataFrame with columns ['x','y','likelihood'] and MultiIndex index:
    # (frame, scorer, individual, bodypart)

    long = long.reset_index()
    long = long.rename(
        columns={
            "level_0": "frame",  # sometimes unnamed; reset_index names can vary
        }
    )

    # Robust rename based on expected index columns:
    # pandas will name them after df.index.name / df.columns.names if present.
    # We'll normalize by position:
    # columns now should be: [frame, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood] in some order.
    # Identify coord columns:
    coord_cols = ["x", "y", "likelihood"]
    for c in coord_cols:
        if c not in long.columns:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Stacked output missing '{c}'. Columns: {list(long.columns)}")

    # Find the non-coord id columns (should be 4 of them)
    id_cols = [c for c in long.columns if c not in coord_cols]
    if len(id_cols) != 4:
        # Fallback: assume first 4 are identifiers if unexpected naming
        id_cols = list(long.columns[:4])

    # Normalize names:
    # Try to map id_cols to frame/scorer/individual/bodypart by content
    # We assume frame is numeric-like and comes first.
    frame_col = id_cols[0]
    scorer_col = id_cols[1]
    individual_col = id_cols[2]
    bodypart_col = id_cols[3]

    long = long.rename(
        columns={
            frame_col: "frame",
            scorer_col: "scorer",
            individual_col: "individual",
            bodypart_col: "bodypart",
        }
    )

    long.insert(1, "camera", camera)
    # Ensure frame is int (or at least numeric)
    long["frame"] = pd.to_numeric(long["frame"], errors="coerce").astype("Int64")

    return long[["frame", "camera", "scorer", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"]]


@dataclass
class DLCPredictions:
    """
    Container for multi-camera DLC predictions.
    """
    long: pd.DataFrame
    cameras: List[str]
    individuals: List[str]
    bodyparts: List[str]
    scorer: str
    frames: int

    def to_array(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Return dense array of shape (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood).
        Missing entries remain NaN.
        """
        T = self.frames
        C = len(self.cameras)
        I = len(self.individuals)
        B = len(self.bodyparts)

        arr = np.full((T, C, I, B, 3), np.nan, dtype=np.float32)

        cam_index = {c: i for i, c in enumerate(self.cameras)}
        ind_index = {m: i for i, m in enumerate(self.individuals)}
        bp_index = {b: i for i, b in enumerate(self.bodyparts)}

        df = self.long
        # Drop rows with unknown frame or out-of-range frames
        df = df.dropna(subset=["frame"])
        df = df[df["frame"].between(0, T - 1)]

        for row in df.itertuples(index=False):
            t = int(row.frame)
            c = cam_index[row.camera]
            i = ind_index[row.individual]
            b = bp_index[row.bodypart]
            arr[t, c, i, b, 0] = float(row.x)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 1] = float(row.y)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 2] = float(row.likelihood)

        return arr


def load_dlc_multicam_el(
    camera_to_h5: Dict[str, str | Path],
    *,
    require_same_frames: bool = True,
) -> DLCPredictions:
    """
    Load multiple *_el.h5 files (one per camera) and return normalized predictions.

    Args:
      camera_to_h5: mapping like {"cam1_top": "..._el.h5", ...}
      require_same_frames: if True, assert all cameras have same number of frames.

    Returns:
      DLCPredictions (long df + metadata + helper to build a dense array)
    """
    if not camera_to_h5:
        raise ValueError("camera_to_h5 is empty")

    longs = []
    frame_counts = {}
    scorer_names = set()

    for cam, path in camera_to_h5.items():
        df = _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(path)
        df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

        # Basic metadata
        frame_counts[cam] = len(df.index)
        scorer_names.update(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(0)))

        longs.append(_stack_one_camera(df, camera=cam))

    long = pd.concat(longs, ignore_index=True)

    # Determine canonical scorer (usually only one)
    if len(scorer_names) == 0:
        scorer = ""
    elif len(scorer_names) == 1:
        scorer = next(iter(scorer_names))
    else:
        # Keep all, but prefer the first for metadata
        scorer = sorted(scorer_names)[0]

    # Canonical orderings
    cameras = list(camera_to_h5.keys())
    individuals = sorted(long["individual"].dropna().unique().tolist())
    bodyparts = sorted(long["bodypart"].dropna().unique().tolist())

    # Frame consistency
    if require_same_frames:
        counts = set(frame_counts.values())
        if len(counts) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f"Frame counts differ across cameras: {frame_counts}")
        frames = next(iter(counts))
    else:
        frames = max(frame_counts.values())

    # Cast dtypes
    long["x"] = pd.to_numeric(long["x"], errors="coerce")
    long["y"] = pd.to_numeric(long["y"], errors="coerce")
    long["likelihood"] = pd.to_numeric(long["likelihood"], errors="coerce")

    return DLCPredictions(
        long=long,
        cameras=cameras,
        individuals=individuals,
        bodyparts=bodyparts,
        scorer=scorer,
        frames=frames,
    )
```

### Example usage (your case)
```python
from dlc_read_multicam import load_dlc_multicam_el

camera_to_h5 = {
    "cam1_top":   "/.../dlc_predictions/cam1_topDLC_..._el.h5",
    "cam2_front": "/.../dlc_predictions/cam2_frontDLC_..._el.h5",
    "cam3_side":  "/.../dlc_predictions/cam3_sideDLC_..._el.h5",
}

pred = load_dlc_multicam_el(camera_to_h5)

print(pred.frames, pred.cameras, pred.individuals, pred.bodyparts)
df_long = pred.long                # long-format table
arr = pred.to_array()              # (T, C, I, B, 3) -> x,y,likelihood
```

path = "/mnt/data/dlc_read_multicam_cli.py"
code = r'''#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
dlc_read_multicam_cli.py

Standalone CLI utility to load multi-camera multi-animal DeepLabCut outputs
(e.g., *_el.h5) and export:

1) A long-format table (CSV/Parquet) with one row per:
   (frame, camera, individual, bodypart) -> x, y, likelihood

2) Optionally a dense NumPy array saved as NPZ:
   arr shape = (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood)

Assumes DLC multi-animal H5 columns are a 4-level MultiIndex:
  (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord) where coord in {'x','y','likelihood'}.

Examples:
  python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \
    --input cam1_top:/path/cam1_top*_el.h5 \
    --input cam2_front:/path/cam2_front*_el.h5 \
    --input cam3_side:/path/cam3_side*_el.h5 \
    --out-long /tmp/dlc_long.csv \
    --out-npz /tmp/dlc_array.npz

If you provide globs, the script will expand them; each camera must resolve to exactly
one file.
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd


def _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(h5_path: str | Path) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    DLC writes H5 in different keys depending on the function/path.
    For *_el.h5, pd.read_hdf(path) often works directly.
    This helper falls back to reading the first key that is a DataFrame.
    """
    h5_path = str(h5_path)
    try:
        df = pd.read_hdf(h5_path)
        if isinstance(df, pd.DataFrame):
            return df
    except (ValueError, KeyError):
        pass

    with pd.HDFStore(h5_path, mode="r") as store:
        for key in store.keys():
            obj = store.get(key)
            if isinstance(obj, pd.DataFrame):
                return obj

    raise RuntimeError(f"No DataFrame found in H5 file: {h5_path}")


def _ensure_expected_multindex(df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Ensure df.columns is a 4-level MultiIndex:
      level0: scorer
      level1: individual
      level2: bodypart
      level3: coord in {'x','y','likelihood'}
    """
    if not isinstance(df.columns, pd.MultiIndex) or df.columns.nlevels != 4:
        raise ValueError(
            "Expected 4-level MultiIndex columns "
            "(scorer, individual, bodypart, coord). "
            f"Got: {type(df.columns)} with nlevels={getattr(df.columns, 'nlevels', None)}"
        )

    coords = set(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(3)))
    needed = {"x", "y", "likelihood"}
    if not needed.issubset(coords):
        raise ValueError(f"Expected coord level to contain {needed}, got {sorted(coords)}")

    return df


def _stack_one_camera(df: pd.DataFrame, camera: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    """
    Convert wide DLC MultiIndex df to long format:
      frame, camera, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood
    """
    df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

    # Stack to long: index -> frame, columns -> multiindex (scorer, individual, bodypart)
    long = df.stack(level=[0, 1, 2])  # leaves coord as columns (x/y/likelihood)
    long = long.reset_index()

    coord_cols = ["x", "y", "likelihood"]
    for c in coord_cols:
        if c not in long.columns:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Stacked output missing '{c}'. Columns: {list(long.columns)}")

    # Identify the 4 identifier columns (frame + 3 stacked levels)
    id_cols = [c for c in long.columns if c not in coord_cols]
    if len(id_cols) != 4:
        # Fallback: assume the first 4 are identifiers
        id_cols = list(long.columns[:4])

    frame_col, scorer_col, individual_col, bodypart_col = id_cols

    long = long.rename(
        columns={
            frame_col: "frame",
            scorer_col: "scorer",
            individual_col: "individual",
            bodypart_col: "bodypart",
        }
    )
    long.insert(1, "camera", camera)

    # Ensure numeric frame index
    long["frame"] = pd.to_numeric(long["frame"], errors="coerce").astype("Int64")

    return long[["frame", "camera", "scorer", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"]]


@dataclass
class DLCPredictions:
    long: pd.DataFrame
    cameras: List[str]
    individuals: List[str]
    bodyparts: List[str]
    scorer: str
    frames: int

    def to_array(self) -> np.ndarray:
        """
        Dense array shape: (T, C, I, B, 3) where last dim is (x, y, likelihood).
        """
        T = self.frames
        C = len(self.cameras)
        I = len(self.individuals)
        B = len(self.bodyparts)

        arr = np.full((T, C, I, B, 3), np.nan, dtype=np.float32)

        cam_index = {c: i for i, c in enumerate(self.cameras)}
        ind_index = {m: i for i, m in enumerate(self.individuals)}
        bp_index = {b: i for i, b in enumerate(self.bodyparts)}

        df = self.long.dropna(subset=["frame"])
        df = df[df["frame"].between(0, T - 1)]

        for row in df.itertuples(index=False):
            t = int(row.frame)
            c = cam_index[row.camera]
            i = ind_index[row.individual]
            b = bp_index[row.bodypart]
            arr[t, c, i, b, 0] = float(row.x)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 1] = float(row.y)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 2] = float(row.likelihood)

        return arr


def load_dlc_multicam_el(
    camera_to_h5: Dict[str, str | Path],
    *,
    require_same_frames: bool = True,
    pcutoff: Optional[float] = None,
) -> DLCPredictions:
    """
    Load multiple *_el.h5 files (one per camera) and return normalized predictions.
    """
    if not camera_to_h5:
        raise ValueError("camera_to_h5 is empty")

    longs: List[pd.DataFrame] = []
    frame_counts: Dict[str, int] = {}
    scorer_names: set[str] = set()

    for cam, path in camera_to_h5.items():
        df = _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(path)
        df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

        frame_counts[cam] = len(df.index)
        scorer_names.update(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(0)))

        longs.append(_stack_one_camera(df, camera=cam))

    long = pd.concat(longs, ignore_index=True)

    # Optional pcutoff filter (keep rows; you can also keep but mark low likelihood)
    if pcutoff is not None:
        long.loc[long["likelihood"] < float(pcutoff), ["x", "y"]] = np.nan

    # Determine canonical scorer (usually only one)
    if len(scorer_names) == 1:
        scorer = next(iter(scorer_names))
    elif len(scorer_names) == 0:
        scorer = ""
    else:
        scorer = sorted(scorer_names)[0]

    cameras = list(camera_to_h5.keys())
    individuals = sorted(long["individual"].dropna().unique().tolist())
    bodyparts = sorted(long["bodypart"].dropna().unique().tolist())

    if require_same_frames:
        counts = set(frame_counts.values())
        if len(counts) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f"Frame counts differ across cameras: {frame_counts}")
        frames = next(iter(counts))
    else:
        frames = max(frame_counts.values())

    long["x"] = pd.to_numeric(long["x"], errors="coerce")
    long["y"] = pd.to_numeric(long["y"], errors="coerce")
    long["likelihood"] = pd.to_numeric(long["likelihood"], errors="coerce")

    return DLCPredictions(
        long=long,
        cameras=cameras,
        individuals=individuals,
        bodyparts=bodyparts,
        scorer=scorer,
        frames=frames,
    )


def _parse_input_specs(specs: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Path]:
    """
    Parse --input items of the form:
      camname:/path/to/file_or_glob.h5
    Globs must resolve to exactly one file per camera.
    """
    out: Dict[str, Path] = {}
    for s in specs:
        if ":" not in s:
            raise ValueError(f"--input must be 'camera:/path' but got: {s}")
        cam, p = s.split(":", 1)
        cam = cam.strip()
        p = p.strip()
        if not cam:
            raise ValueError(f"Empty camera name in --input: {s}")
        matches = sorted(Path().glob(p)) if any(ch in p for ch in ["*", "?", "["]) else [Path(p)]
        matches = [m for m in matches if m.exists()]
        if len(matches) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f"--input {cam}:{p} resolved to {len(matches)} files: {matches}")
        out[cam] = matches[0].resolve()
    return out


def _write_long(df: pd.DataFrame, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    suffix = out_path.suffix.lower()
    if suffix in [".csv", ".txt"]:
        df.to_csv(out_path, index=False)
    elif suffix in [".parquet"]:
        try:
            import pyarrow  # noqa: F401
        except Exception as e:
            raise RuntimeError("Parquet output requires 'pyarrow'. Install it or use .csv") from e
        df.to_parquet(out_path, index=False)
    else:
        raise ValueError(f"Unsupported --out-long extension '{suffix}'. Use .csv or .parquet")


def _write_npz(pred: DLCPredictions, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    arr = pred.to_array()
    np.savez_compressed(
        out_path,
        arr=arr,
        cameras=np.array(pred.cameras, dtype=object),
        individuals=np.array(pred.individuals, dtype=object),
        bodyparts=np.array(pred.bodyparts, dtype=object),
        scorer=np.array(pred.scorer, dtype=object),
    )


def main() -> None:
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description="Load multi-camera DeepLabCut multi-animal *_el.h5 outputs and export normalized data."
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        "--input",
        action="append",
        required=True,
        help="Repeatable. Format: camname:/path/to/file_or_glob_el.h5 (globs must match exactly one file).",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        "--out-long",
        type=str,
        default="",
        help="Output path for long-format table (.csv or .parquet). If omitted, no table is written.",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        "--out-npz",
        type=str,
        default="",
        help="Output path for dense array NPZ (arr shape (T,C,I,B,3)). If omitted, no array is written.",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        "--pcutoff",
        type=float,
        default=None,
        help="If set, rows with likelihood < pcutoff will have x/y set to NaN.",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        "--allow-different-frames",
        action="store_true",
        help="Allow cameras to have different number of frames; array T becomes max over cameras.",
    )

    args = ap.parse_args()

    camera_to_h5 = _parse_input_specs(args.input)

    pred = load_dlc_multicam_el(
        camera_to_h5,
        require_same_frames=(not args.allow_different_frames),
        pcutoff=args.pcutoff,
    )

    # Print summary
    print("Loaded DLC predictions:")
    print("  cameras:", pred.cameras)
    print("  individuals:", pred.individuals)
    print("  bodyparts:", pred.bodyparts)
    print("  frames:", pred.frames)
    print("  scorer:", pred.scorer)
    print("  long shape:", pred.long.shape)

    if args.out_long:
        out_path = Path(args.out_long).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_long(pred.long, out_path)
        print("Wrote long table:", out_path)

    if args.out_npz:
        out_path = Path(args.out_npz).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_npz(pred, out_path)
        print("Wrote NPZ array:", out_path)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
'''

Assistant: import os
from pathlib import Path

path = "/mnt/data/dlc_read_multicam_cli.py"
code = """#!/usr/bin/env python3
\"\"\"
dlc_read_multicam_cli.py

Standalone CLI utility to load multi-camera multi-animal DeepLabCut outputs
(e.g., *_el.h5) and export:

1) A long-format table (CSV/Parquet) with one row per:
   (frame, camera, individual, bodypart) -> x, y, likelihood

2) Optionally a dense NumPy array saved as NPZ:
   arr shape = (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood)

Assumes DLC multi-animal H5 columns are a 4-level MultiIndex:
  (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord) where coord in {'x','y','likelihood'}.

Examples:
  python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \\
    --input cam1_top:/path/cam1_top*_el.h5 \\
    --input cam2_front:/path/cam2_front*_el.h5 \\
    --input cam3_side:/path/cam3_side*_el.h5 \\
    --out-long /tmp/dlc_long.csv \\
    --out-npz /tmp/dlc_array.npz

If you provide globs, the script will expand them; each camera must resolve to exactly
one file.
\"\"\"

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd


def _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(h5_path: str | Path) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Read the first DataFrame from an HDF5 file (handles varying keys).\"\"\"
    h5_path = str(h5_path)
    try:
        df = pd.read_hdf(h5_path)
        if isinstance(df, pd.DataFrame):
            return df
    except (ValueError, KeyError):
        pass

    with pd.HDFStore(h5_path, mode="r") as store:
        for key in store.keys():
            obj = store.get(key)
            if isinstance(obj, pd.DataFrame):
                return obj

    raise RuntimeError(f"No DataFrame found in H5 file: {h5_path}")


def _ensure_expected_multindex(df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Validate DLC multi-animal MultiIndex columns: (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord).\"\"\"
    if not isinstance(df.columns, pd.MultiIndex) or df.columns.nlevels != 4:
        raise ValueError(
            "Expected 4-level MultiIndex columns (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord). "
            f"Got: {type(df.columns)} with nlevels={getattr(df.columns, 'nlevels', None)}"
        )

    coords = set(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(3)))
    needed = {"x", "y", "likelihood"}
    if not needed.issubset(coords):
        raise ValueError(f"Expected coord level to contain {needed}, got {sorted(coords)}")

    return df


def _stack_one_camera(df: pd.DataFrame, camera: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Wide -> long: frame, camera, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood.\"\"\"
    df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

    long = df.stack(level=[0, 1, 2])  # leaves coord as columns
    long = long.reset_index()

    coord_cols = ["x", "y", "likelihood"]
    for c in coord_cols:
        if c not in long.columns:
            raise RuntimeError(f"Stacked output missing '{c}'. Columns: {list(long.columns)}")

    id_cols = [c for c in long.columns if c not in coord_cols]
    if len(id_cols) != 4:
        id_cols = list(long.columns[:4])

    frame_col, scorer_col, individual_col, bodypart_col = id_cols
    long = long.rename(
        columns={
            frame_col: "frame",
            scorer_col: "scorer",
            individual_col: "individual",
            bodypart_col: "bodypart",
        }
    )
    long.insert(1, "camera", camera)
    long["frame"] = pd.to_numeric(long["frame"], errors="coerce").astype("Int64")

    return long[["frame", "camera", "scorer", "individual", "bodypart", "x", "y", "likelihood"]]


@dataclass
class DLCPredictions:
    long: pd.DataFrame
    cameras: List[str]
    individuals: List[str]
    bodyparts: List[str]
    scorer: str
    frames: int

    def to_array(self) -> np.ndarray:
        \"\"\"Dense array shape: (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood).\"\"\"
        T = self.frames
        C = len(self.cameras)
        I = len(self.individuals)
        B = len(self.bodyparts)

        arr = np.full((T, C, I, B, 3), np.nan, dtype=np.float32)
        cam_index = {c: i for i, c in enumerate(self.cameras)}
        ind_index = {m: i for i, m in enumerate(self.individuals)}
        bp_index = {b: i for i, b in enumerate(self.bodyparts)}

        df = self.long.dropna(subset=["frame"])
        df = df[df["frame"].between(0, T - 1)]

        for row in df.itertuples(index=False):
            t = int(row.frame)
            c = cam_index[row.camera]
            i = ind_index[row.individual]
            b = bp_index[row.bodypart]
            arr[t, c, i, b, 0] = float(row.x)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 1] = float(row.y)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 2] = float(row.likelihood)

        return arr


def load_dlc_multicam_el(
    camera_to_h5: Dict[str, str | Path],
    *,
    require_same_frames: bool = True,
    pcutoff: Optional[float] = None,
) -> DLCPredictions:
    \"\"\"Load multiple *_el.h5 files (one per camera) and return normalized predictions.\"\"\"
    if not camera_to_h5:
        raise ValueError("camera_to_h5 is empty")

    longs: List[pd.DataFrame] = []
    frame_counts: Dict[str, int] = {}
    scorer_names: set[str] = set()

    for cam, path in camera_to_h5.items():
        df = _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(path)
        df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

        frame_counts[cam] = len(df.index)
        scorer_names.update(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(0)))
        longs.append(_stack_one_camera(df, camera=cam))

    long = pd.concat(longs, ignore_index=True)

    if pcutoff is not None:
        long.loc[long["likelihood"] < float(pcutoff), ["x", "y"]] = np.nan

    if len(scorer_names) == 1:
        scorer = next(iter(scorer_names))
    elif len(scorer_names) == 0:
        scorer = ""
    else:
        scorer = sorted(scorer_names)[0]

    cameras = list(camera_to_h5.keys())
    individuals = sorted(long["individual"].dropna().unique().tolist())
    bodyparts = sorted(long["bodypart"].dropna().unique().tolist())

    if require_same_frames:
        counts = set(frame_counts.values())
        if len(counts) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f"Frame counts differ across cameras: {frame_counts}")
        frames = next(iter(counts))
    else:
        frames = max(frame_counts.values())

    long["x"] = pd.to_numeric(long["x"], errors="coerce")
    long["y"] = pd.to_numeric(long["y"], errors="coerce")
    long["likelihood"] = pd.to_numeric(long["likelihood"], errors="coerce")

    return DLCPredictions(
        long=long,
        cameras=cameras,
        individuals=individuals,
        bodyparts=bodyparts,
        scorer=scorer,
        frames=frames,
    )


def _parse_input_specs(specs: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Path]:
    \"\"\"Parse --input items camname:/path/to/file_or_glob.h5 (globs must match exactly one).\"\"\"
    out: Dict[str, Path] = {}
    for s in specs:
        if ":" not in s:
            raise ValueError(f\"--input must be 'camera:/path' but got: {s}\")
        cam, p = s.split(":", 1)
        cam = cam.strip()
        p = p.strip()
        if not cam:
            raise ValueError(f\"Empty camera name in --input: {s}\")

        is_glob = any(ch in p for ch in ["*", "?", "["])
        matches = sorted(Path().glob(p)) if is_glob else [Path(p)]
        matches = [m for m in matches if m.exists()]
        if len(matches) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f\"--input {cam}:{p} resolved to {len(matches)} files: {matches}\")
        out[cam] = matches[0].resolve()
    return out


def _write_long(df: pd.DataFrame, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    suffix = out_path.suffix.lower()
    if suffix in [".csv", ".txt"]:
        df.to_csv(out_path, index=False)
    elif suffix == ".parquet":
        try:
            import pyarrow  # noqa: F401
        except Exception as e:
            raise RuntimeError(\"Parquet output requires 'pyarrow'. Install it or use .csv\") from e
        df.to_parquet(out_path, index=False)
    else:
        raise ValueError(f\"Unsupported --out-long extension '{suffix}'. Use .csv or .parquet\")


def _write_npz(pred: DLCPredictions, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    arr = pred.to_array()
    np.savez_compressed(
        out_path,
        arr=arr,
        cameras=np.array(pred.cameras, dtype=object),
        individuals=np.array(pred.individuals, dtype=object),
        bodyparts=np.array(pred.bodyparts, dtype=object),
        scorer=np.array(pred.scorer, dtype=object),
    )


def main() -> None:
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description=\"Load multi-camera DeepLabCut multi-animal *_el.h5 outputs and export normalized data.\"
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--input\",
        action=\"append\",
        required=True,
        help=\"Repeatable. Format: camname:/path/to/file_or_glob_el.h5 (glob must match exactly one file).\",\n    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--out-long\",
        type=str,
        default=\"\",
        help=\"Output path for long-format table (.csv or .parquet). If omitted, no table is written.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--out-npz\",
        type=str,
        default=\"\",
        help=\"Output path for dense array NPZ (arr shape (T,C,I,B,3)). If omitted, no array is written.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--pcutoff\",
        type=float,
        default=None,
        help=\"If set, rows with likelihood < pcutoff will have x/y set to NaN.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--allow-different-frames\",
        action=\"store_true\",
        help=\"Allow cameras to have different number of frames; array T becomes max over cameras.\",
    )
    args = ap.parse_args()

    camera_to_h5 = _parse_input_specs(args.input)

    pred = load_dlc_multicam_el(
        camera_to_h5,
        require_same_frames=(not args.allow_different_frames),
        pcutoff=args.pcutoff,
    )

    print(\"Loaded DLC predictions:\")
    print(\"  cameras:\", pred.cameras)
    print(\"  individuals:\", pred.individuals)
    print(\"  bodyparts:\", pred.bodyparts)
    print(\"  frames:\", pred.frames)
    print(\"  scorer:\", pred.scorer)
    print(\"  long shape:\", pred.long.shape)

    if args.out_long:
        out_path = Path(args.out_long).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_long(pred.long, out_path)
        print(\"Wrote long table:\", out_path)

    if args.out_npz:
        out_path = Path(args.out_npz).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_npz(pred, out_path)
        print(\"Wrote NPZ array:\", out_path)


if __name__ == \"__main__\":
    main()
"""
Path(path).write_text(code)
os.chmod(path, 0o755)

Assistant: Here you go — I turned it into a standalone CLI script:

- [Download dlc_read_multicam_cli.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/dlc_read_multicam_cli.py)

## Usage

### 1) Export long-format CSV (recommended first)
```bash
python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \
  --input cam1_top:/media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions/cam1_top*el.h5 \
  --input cam2_front:/media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions/cam2_front*el.h5 \
  --input cam3_side:/media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/mouse_sim/out2m_2_render/dlc_predictions/cam3_side*el.h5 \
  --out-long /tmp/dlc_long.csv
```

### 2) Also export a dense NPZ array `(T,C,I,B,3)`
```bash
python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \
  --input cam1_top:/.../cam1_top*el.h5 \
  --input cam2_front:/.../cam2_front*el.h5 \
  --input cam3_side:/.../cam3_side*el.h5 \
  --out-long /tmp/dlc_long.csv \
  --out-npz /tmp/dlc_array.npz
```

### 3) Apply a likelihood cutoff (set low-likelihood x/y to NaN)
```bash
python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \
  --input cam1_top:/.../cam1_top*el.h5 \
  --input cam2_front:/.../cam2_front*el.h5 \
  --input cam3_side:/.../cam3_side*el.h5 \
  --pcutoff 0.6 \
  --out-long /tmp/dlc_long_p06.csv
```

## Notes
- `--input` can take **globs**, but each camera must match **exactly one file**.
- Default behavior requires all cameras to have the **same number of frames**. If needed:
  - add `--allow-different-frames`

If you tell me what output format you want for your future triangulation step (e.g., one CSV per camera vs. a single merged CSV with camera columns), I can add an export mode that writes exactly that.

import os, textwrap, re

path = "/mnt/data/dlc_read_multicam_cli.py"

# Read existing file
src = Path(path).read_text()

# We'll replace _parse_input_specs function with a version that supports absolute globs via glob.glob
import_pattern = "import argparse"
if "import glob" not in src:
    src = src.replace(import_pattern, import_pattern + "\nimport glob\nimport os\n")

# Replace function body using regex
new_func = r'''
def _parse_input_specs(specs: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Path]:
    """
    Parse --input items of the form:
      camname:/path/to/file_or_glob.h5

    Supports absolute and relative globs. Each camera must resolve to exactly one file.

    Note: pathlib.Path().glob does not support absolute patterns, so we use glob.glob.
    """
    out: Dict[str, Path] = {}
    for s in specs:
        if ":" not in s:
            raise ValueError(f"--input must be 'camera:/path' but got: {s}")
        cam, p = s.split(":", 1)
        cam = cam.strip()
        p = p.strip()
        if not cam:
            raise ValueError(f"Empty camera name in --input: {s}")
        if not p:
            raise ValueError(f"Empty path in --input: {s}")

        # Expand ~ and environment variables
        p_expanded = os.path.expandvars(os.path.expanduser(p))

        is_glob = any(ch in p_expanded for ch in ["*", "?", "["])
        if is_glob:
            matches = sorted(glob.glob(p_expanded))
            matches = [Path(m) for m in matches]
        else:
            matches = [Path(p_expanded)]

        matches = [m for m in matches if m.exists()]
        if len(matches) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f"--input {cam}:{p} resolved to {len(matches)} files: {matches}")
        out[cam] = matches[0].resolve()
    return out
'''

src2 = re.sub(r"def _parse_input_specs\(specs: List\[str\]\) -> Dict\[str, Path\]:.*?return out\n",
              new_func.strip() + "\n",
              src,
              flags=re.S)

Path(path).write_text(src2)

code = """#!/usr/bin/env python3
\"\"\"
dlc_read_multicam_cli.py

Standalone CLI utility to load multi-camera multi-animal DeepLabCut outputs
(e.g., *_el.h5) and export:

1) A long-format table (CSV/Parquet) with one row per:
   (frame, camera, individual, bodypart) -> x, y, likelihood

2) Optionally a dense NumPy array saved as NPZ:
   arr shape = (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood)

Assumes DLC multi-animal H5 columns are a 4-level MultiIndex:
  (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord) where coord in {'x','y','likelihood'}.

Examples:
  python dlc_read_multicam_cli.py \\
    --input cam1_top:/path/cam1_top*_el.h5 \\
    --input cam2_front:/path/cam2_front*_el.h5 \\
    --input cam3_side:/path/cam3_side*_el.h5 \\
    --out-long /tmp/dlc_long.csv \\
    --out-npz /tmp/dlc_array.npz

Globs may be absolute or relative; each camera must resolve to exactly one file.
\"\"\"

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import glob
import os
from dataclasses import dataclass
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd


def _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(h5_path: str | Path) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Read the first DataFrame from an HDF5 file (handles varying keys).\"\"\"
    h5_path = str(h5_path)
    try:
        df = pd.read_hdf(h5_path)
        if isinstance(df, pd.DataFrame):
            return df
    except (ValueError, KeyError):
        pass

    with pd.HDFStore(h5_path, mode=\"r\") as store:
        for key in store.keys():
            obj = store.get(key)
            if isinstance(obj, pd.DataFrame):
                return obj

    raise RuntimeError(f\"No DataFrame found in H5 file: {h5_path}\")


def _ensure_expected_multindex(df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Validate DLC multi-animal MultiIndex columns: (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord).\"\"\"
    if not isinstance(df.columns, pd.MultiIndex) or df.columns.nlevels != 4:
        raise ValueError(
            \"Expected 4-level MultiIndex columns (scorer, individual, bodypart, coord). \"
            f\"Got: {type(df.columns)} with nlevels={getattr(df.columns, 'nlevels', None)}\"
        )

    coords = set(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(3)))
    needed = {\"x\", \"y\", \"likelihood\"}
    if not needed.issubset(coords):
        raise ValueError(f\"Expected coord level to contain {needed}, got {sorted(coords)}\")

    return df


def _stack_one_camera(df: pd.DataFrame, camera: str) -> pd.DataFrame:
    \"\"\"Wide -> long: frame, camera, scorer, individual, bodypart, x, y, likelihood.\"\"\"
    df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

    long = df.stack(level=[0, 1, 2])  # leaves coord as columns
    long = long.reset_index()

    coord_cols = [\"x\", \"y\", \"likelihood\"]
    for c in coord_cols:
        if c not in long.columns:
            raise RuntimeError(f\"Stacked output missing '{c}'. Columns: {list(long.columns)}\")

    id_cols = [c for c in long.columns if c not in coord_cols]
    if len(id_cols) != 4:
        id_cols = list(long.columns[:4])

    frame_col, scorer_col, individual_col, bodypart_col = id_cols
    long = long.rename(
        columns={
            frame_col: \"frame\",
            scorer_col: \"scorer\",
            individual_col: \"individual\",
            bodypart_col: \"bodypart\",
        }
    )
    long.insert(1, \"camera\", camera)
    long[\"frame\"] = pd.to_numeric(long[\"frame\"], errors=\"coerce\").astype(\"Int64\")

    return long[[\"frame\", \"camera\", \"scorer\", \"individual\", \"bodypart\", \"x\", \"y\", \"likelihood\"]]


@dataclass
class DLCPredictions:
    long: pd.DataFrame
    cameras: List[str]
    individuals: List[str]
    bodyparts: List[str]
    scorer: str
    frames: int

    def to_array(self) -> np.ndarray:
        \"\"\"Dense array shape: (T, C, I, B, 3) with (x, y, likelihood).\"\"\"
        T = self.frames
        C = len(self.cameras)
        I = len(self.individuals)
        B = len(self.bodyparts)

        arr = np.full((T, C, I, B, 3), np.nan, dtype=np.float32)
        cam_index = {c: i for i, c in enumerate(self.cameras)}
        ind_index = {m: i for i, m in enumerate(self.individuals)}
        bp_index = {b: i for i, b in enumerate(self.bodyparts)}

        df = self.long.dropna(subset=[\"frame\"])
        df = df[df[\"frame\"].between(0, T - 1)]

        for row in df.itertuples(index=False):
            t = int(row.frame)
            c = cam_index[row.camera]
            i = ind_index[row.individual]
            b = bp_index[row.bodypart]
            arr[t, c, i, b, 0] = float(row.x)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 1] = float(row.y)
            arr[t, c, i, b, 2] = float(row.likelihood)

        return arr


def load_dlc_multicam_el(
    camera_to_h5: Dict[str, str | Path],
    *,
    require_same_frames: bool = True,
    pcutoff: Optional[float] = None,
) -> DLCPredictions:
    \"\"\"Load multiple *_el.h5 files (one per camera) and return normalized predictions.\"\"\"
    if not camera_to_h5:
        raise ValueError(\"camera_to_h5 is empty\")

    longs: List[pd.DataFrame] = []
    frame_counts: Dict[str, int] = {}
    scorer_names: set[str] = set()

    for cam, path in camera_to_h5.items():
        df = _read_first_dataframe_from_h5(path)
        df = _ensure_expected_multindex(df)

        frame_counts[cam] = len(df.index)
        scorer_names.update(map(str, df.columns.get_level_values(0)))
        longs.append(_stack_one_camera(df, camera=cam))

    long = pd.concat(longs, ignore_index=True)

    if pcutoff is not None:
        long.loc[long[\"likelihood\"] < float(pcutoff), [\"x\", \"y\"]] = np.nan

    if len(scorer_names) == 1:
        scorer = next(iter(scorer_names))
    elif len(scorer_names) == 0:
        scorer = \"\"
    else:
        scorer = sorted(scorer_names)[0]

    cameras = list(camera_to_h5.keys())
    individuals = sorted(long[\"individual\"].dropna().unique().tolist())
    bodyparts = sorted(long[\"bodypart\"].dropna().unique().tolist())

    if require_same_frames:
        counts = set(frame_counts.values())
        if len(counts) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f\"Frame counts differ across cameras: {frame_counts}\")
        frames = next(iter(counts))
    else:
        frames = max(frame_counts.values())

    long[\"x\"] = pd.to_numeric(long[\"x\"], errors=\"coerce\")
    long[\"y\"] = pd.to_numeric(long[\"y\"], errors=\"coerce\")
    long[\"likelihood\"] = pd.to_numeric(long[\"likelihood\"], errors=\"coerce\")

    return DLCPredictions(
        long=long,
        cameras=cameras,
        individuals=individuals,
        bodyparts=bodyparts,
        scorer=scorer,
        frames=frames,
    )


def _parse_input_specs(specs: List[str]) -> Dict[str, Path]:
    \"\"\"
    Parse --input items of the form:
      camname:/path/to/file_or_glob.h5

    Supports absolute and relative globs. Each camera must resolve to exactly one file.
    \"\"\"
    out: Dict[str, Path] = {}
    for s in specs:
        if \":\" not in s:
            raise ValueError(f\"--input must be 'camera:/path' but got: {s}\")
        cam, p = s.split(\":\", 1)
        cam = cam.strip()
        p = p.strip()
        if not cam:
            raise ValueError(f\"Empty camera name in --input: {s}\")
        if not p:
            raise ValueError(f\"Empty path in --input: {s}\")

        # Expand ~ and environment variables
        p_expanded = os.path.expandvars(os.path.expanduser(p))

        is_glob = any(ch in p_expanded for ch in [\"*\", \"?\", \"[\"])
        if is_glob:
            matches = sorted(glob.glob(p_expanded))
            matches = [Path(m) for m in matches]
        else:
            matches = [Path(p_expanded)]

        matches = [m for m in matches if m.exists()]
        if len(matches) != 1:
            raise ValueError(f\"--input {cam}:{p} resolved to {len(matches)} files: {matches}\")
        out[cam] = matches[0].resolve()
    return out


def _write_long(df: pd.DataFrame, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    suffix = out_path.suffix.lower()
    if suffix in [\".csv\", \".txt\"]:
        df.to_csv(out_path, index=False)
    elif suffix == \".parquet\":
        try:
            import pyarrow  # noqa: F401
        except Exception as e:
            raise RuntimeError(\"Parquet output requires 'pyarrow'. Install it or use .csv\") from e
        df.to_parquet(out_path, index=False)
    else:
        raise ValueError(f\"Unsupported --out-long extension '{suffix}'. Use .csv or .parquet\")


def _write_npz(pred: DLCPredictions, out_path: Path) -> None:
    out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    arr = pred.to_array()
    np.savez_compressed(
        out_path,
        arr=arr,
        cameras=np.array(pred.cameras, dtype=object),
        individuals=np.array(pred.individuals, dtype=object),
        bodyparts=np.array(pred.bodyparts, dtype=object),
        scorer=np.array(pred.scorer, dtype=object),
    )


def main() -> None:
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description=\"Load multi-camera DeepLabCut multi-animal *_el.h5 outputs and export normalized data.\"
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--input\",
        action=\"append\",
        required=True,
        help=\"Repeatable. Format: camname:/path/to/file_or_glob_el.h5 (glob must match exactly one file).\",\n    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--out-long\",
        type=str,
        default=\"\",
        help=\"Output path for long-format table (.csv or .parquet). If omitted, no table is written.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--out-npz\",
        type=str,
        default=\"\",
        help=\"Output path for dense array NPZ (arr shape (T,C,I,B,3)). If omitted, no array is written.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--pcutoff\",
        type=float,
        default=None,
        help=\"If set, rows with likelihood < pcutoff will have x/y set to NaN.\",
    )
    ap.add_argument(
        \"--allow-different-frames\",
        action=\"store_true\",
        help=\"Allow cameras to have different number of frames; array T becomes max over cameras.\",
    )
    args = ap.parse_args()

    camera_to_h5 = _parse_input_specs(args.input)

    pred = load_dlc_multicam_el(
        camera_to_h5,
        require_same_frames=(not args.allow_different_frames),
        pcutoff=args.pcutoff,
    )

    print(\"Loaded DLC predictions:\")
    print(\"  cameras:\", pred.cameras)
    print(\"  individuals:\", pred.individuals)
    print(\"  bodyparts:\", pred.bodyparts)
    print(\"  frames:\", pred.frames)
    print(\"  scorer:\", pred.scorer)
    print(\"  long shape:\", pred.long.shape)

    if args.out_long:
        out_path = Path(args.out_long).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_long(pred.long, out_path)
        print(\"Wrote long table:\", out_path)

    if args.out_npz:
        out_path = Path(args.out_npz).expanduser().resolve()
        _write_npz(pred, out_path)
        print(\"Wrote NPZ array:\", out_path)


if __name__ == \"__main__\":
    main()
"""

Path(path).write_text(code)
os.chmod(path, 0o755)

Assistant: That other project’s `.h5` files are almost certainly **single-animal DLC outputs**, which use **3 column levels**:

- **(scorer, bodypart, coord)**

Your simulated multi-animal pipeline produced **4 levels**:

- **(scorer, individual, bodypart, coord)**

So your reader failed because it expected 4 levels.

I patched the reader to accept **both 3-level and 4-level DLC H5s** (and some minor level-order permutations). For 3-level files it **inserts a synthetic `individual`** (default: `mouse0`) so the rest of the pipeline stays consistent.

### What this change does (so you can trust it)
- If the H5 columns are **4-level**, it just standardizes the ordering to `(scorer, individual, bodypart, coord)`.
- If the H5 columns are **3-level**, it assumes they mean `(scorer, bodypart, coord)` and inserts `individual=<--default-individual>`.
- Bodypart names can be anything; it just reads whatever is in the file.

Assistant: I wrote a standalone CLI program that overlays **2D DLC points from `dlc_long.csv`** onto your **three camera videos**, draws **skeleton edges from `--template`**, and produces a **joined (side-by-side) mosaic video**—without using `cameras.json` or any reprojection.

**File:** `overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py`  
Path: `/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py`

### Usage example (matches your naming)
```bash
python overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py \
  --dlc-long /path/to/dlc_long.csv \
  --template mouse3_mesh_shortTail.txt \
  --top-in   /path/to/cam1_top.mp4   --top-cam   cam1_top \
  --front-in /path/to/cam2_front.mp4 --front-cam cam2_front \
  --side-in  /path/to/cam3_side.mp4  --side-cam  cam3_side \
  --out-dir  /path/to/out_overlay \
  --pcutoff 0.6
```

- Points with `likelihood >= pcutoff` are drawn as **filled blobs**.
- Points below `pcutoff` are drawn as **hollow circles**.
- Skeleton edges are drawn **only if both endpoints are confident** (>= `pcutoff`).

Optional:
```bash
  --draw-labels
  --radius 5
  --thickness 2
  --ind-colors mouse0:#FF00FF --ind-colors mouse1:0,255,255
```

### Output
Writes:
- `*_dlc_overlay.mp4` for top/front/side into `--out-dir`
- `joined_dlc_overlay.mp4` (3 videos concatenated horizontally)

User: Why would the program need cam files? There are only 2D points to be superimposed to video frames. No 3D to 2D projection required.

Assistant: You’re right: for *this* overlay task (drawing DLC 2D points onto the corresponding 2D video frames), **no camera calibration / `cameras.json` is needed at all**.

If my script interface mentioned “cam files”, that was either:

1) **only to choose which rows from `dlc_long.csv` belong to which video** (e.g., `camera=cam1_top`), and/or  
2) leftover naming from the 3D→2D overlay script style.

### What the overlay actually needs
Minimum inputs:

- **The three videos** (top/front/side) so we have frames to draw on.
- **`dlc_long.csv`** containing at least:
  - `frame` (or time that can be mapped to frame index),
  - `camera` (or some camera identifier),
  - `individual` (optional; multi-animal),
  - `bodypart`,
  - `x`, `y`,
  - `likelihood` (optional but useful),
- **`--template .txt`** only for skeleton edges (bodypart graph), *not* for geometry.
- An output path.

That’s it.

### Why camera *names* still matter (but not camera *files*)
If your `dlc_long.csv` contains predictions from multiple views, the script must know which rows correspond to which video. This can be done by:

- using a `camera` column inside the CSV (best), and mapping e.g. `cam1_top` → that video, **or**
- if there is no camera column, you run the overlay separately per CSV/video, **or**
- you pass a per-input filter like `--top-cam cam1_top` so it selects matching rows.

So: **camera calibration files are unnecessary**, but **a camera identifier** is still useful to route rows to the right video stream.

### If you want it even simpler
If your `dlc_long.csv` **does not include a camera column**, we can make the program accept:

- `--dlc-long-top ... --dlc-long-front ... --dlc-long-side ...`

and completely remove `--*-cam` arguments.

Or, if the CSV *does* include camera, we can drop `--top-cam/--front-cam/--side-cam` and just infer camera names from the video basenames (e.g., `cam1_top.mp4` → `cam1_top`).

If you tell me which of these matches your `dlc_long.csv` format (has `camera` column? and what it’s called), I’ll adjust the script accordingly.

v2 has been renamed to the previous version's name. Then it fails ...

Assistant: That crash is simply because the file you’re *actually running* (`overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py` in your repo) is missing the helper it now calls:

```py
palette = _default_palette()
```

So you ended up with a “hybrid” version (new `main()` calling `_default_palette`, but no `_default_palette` defined).

I fixed this properly by adding `_default_palette()` back in, while keeping the two features you wanted:

- **Frame index** drawn in the **upper-left corner** of each view.
- **Joined video layout** as a 2×2 mosaic:
  - **upper-left**: empty/black
  - **upper-right**: **top**
  - **bottom-left**: **side**
  - **bottom-right**: **front**

Here’s the corrected standalone script:

  --top-cam   cam1_top \
  --front-in /media/hellwich/Herakles/hellwich/hellwich/sdk3/mouseModel/LockBoxModel/labeled/2021-06-18_07-28-45_segment1_mouse291_combined_front-view.avi \
  --front-cam cam2_front \

TypeError: join_three_videos_quadrants() got an unexpected keyword argument 'labels'

Assistant: That crash is just a small API mismatch inside the script:

- `main()` calls `join_three_videos_quadrants(..., labels=(...))`
- but `join_three_videos_quadrants()` in your renamed file doesn’t accept a `labels` keyword → `TypeError`.

I fixed it by:
1) Adding a `labels=...` keyword parameter to `join_three_videos_quadrants` (default `("top","front","side")`), and
2) Actually drawing those labels into the mosaic (optional),
3) Keeping the quadrant layout you wanted (top = upper-right, front = lower-right, side = lower-left), and
4) Keeping frame-index overlay (upper-left corner) on the per-camera outputs.

Download the corrected script here:
[Download overlay_dlc_long_on_videos_v4.py](sandbox:/mnt/data/overlay_dlc_long_on_videos_v4.py)

### Use it (recommended)
Copy it over your current `overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py` in `mouse_sim/`:
```bash
cp overlay_dlc_long_on_videos_v4.py overlay_dlc_long_on_videos.py
```

Then rerun your exact command.

If you want the mosaic labels disabled, you can edit the call in `main()` to:
```python
join_three_videos_quadrants(top_out, front_out, side_out, joined_out, labels=None)
```
